10109{_}2707{_}"It is too much, captain, I tell you it is too much.
10109{_}2708{_}Think what you are doing, and send the black man off."
10109{_}2709{_}"I have been thinking the matter over for some time," replied my father tranquilly, "and I have determined to do the thing thoroughly.
10109{_}2710{_}If he cannot like me, it is better for him to hate me, and may save trouble.
10109{_}2711{_}Tie him up, Brutus."
10109{_}2712{_}"Bear away!"
10109{_}2713{_}cried Mr. Aiken harshly.
10109{_}2714{_}"Mind yourself, sir."
10109{_}2715{_}His warning, however, was late in coming.
10109{_}2716{_}I had sprung at my father before the sentence was finished.
10109{_}2717{_}It was almost the only time I knew him to miscalculate.
10109{_}2718{_}He must have been taken unaware, for he stepped backward too quickly, and collided with the very chair he had quitted.
10109{_}2719{_}It shook his balance for the moment, so that he thrust a hand behind him to recover himself, and in the same instant I had the volume of Rabelais.
10109{_}2720{_}I leapt for the open doorway, but Ned Aiken was there to intercept me.
10109{_}2721{_}Brutus was up behind me with his great hands clamping down on my shoulders.
10109{_}2722{_}I turned and hurled the volume in the fireplace.
10109{_}2723{_}My father caught it out almost before it landed.
10109{_}2724{_}With all the deliberation of a connoisseur examining an old and rare edition, he turned the pages with his slim fingers.
10109{_}2725{_}There, as he had said, was the paper, with the same red seals that I had admired the previous evening.
10109{_}2726{_}He placed it slowly in his inside pocket, and tossed the book on the floor.
10109{_}2727{_}"Now here's a pretty kettle of fish," said Mr. Aiken.
10109{_}2728{_}My father was watching me thoughtfully.
10109{_}2729{_}"Take your hands off him, Brutus," he said, "and bring out the horse."
10109{_}2730{_}For a second longer we stood motionless, each watching the other.
10109{_}2731{_}Then my father crossed to the long table near which I was standing, picked up the pistols that Brutus had left there, and slipped them into his capacious side pockets.
10109{_}2732{_}"You disappoint me, Henry," he remarked.
10109{_}2733{_}"You should have used those pistols."
10109{_}2734{_}"I had thought of them," I answered.
10109{_}2735{_}"I am glad of that," he said.
10109{_}2736{_}"It is a relief to know you did not overlook them.
10109{_}2737{_}You were right, Mademoiselle.
10109{_}2738{_}I should have known better than to treat him so.
10109{_}2739{_}We have ceased to play the game, my son.
10109{_}2740{_}It only remains to take my leave.
10109{_}2741{_}I shall not trouble you again."
10109{_}2742{_}He was standing close beside me.
10109{_}2743{_}Was it possible his eyes were a little wistful, and his voice a trifle sad?
10109{_}2744{_}"I thought I should be glad to leave you," he said, "and somehow I am sorry.
10109{_}2745{_}Odd that we can never properly gauge our emotions.
10109{_}2746{_}I feel that you will be a very blithe and active gentleman in time, and there are not so many left in these drab days.
10109{_}2747{_}Ah, well--"  His sword was lying on the table.
10109{_}2748{_}He drew it, and tucked the naked blade under his arm.
10109{_}2749{_}In spite of the two candles which Brutus had left, the shadows had closed about us, so that his figure alone remained distinct in the yellow light, slender and carelessly elegant.
10109{_}2750{_}I think it pleased him to have us all three watching.
10109{_}2751{_}Any gathering, however small, that he might dominate, appeared to give him enjoyment--his leave taking not less than the others.
10109{_}2752{_}"It is growing dark, Mr. Aiken," he observed, "and our position is not without its drawbacks.
10109{_}2753{_}Call in the men from outside, and take them aboard and give them a measure of rum.
10109{_}2754{_}No one will disturb me before I leave, I think.
10109{_}2755{_}You had better weigh at once, and never mind your running lights till it is time for them."
10109{_}2756{_}"So you're going to do it," said Mr. Aiken.
10109{_}2757{_}"I might have known you wouldn't listen to reason."
10109{_}2758{_}"You should have sailed with me long enough," said my father, "to know I never do."
10109{_}2759{_}"And you not even dressed for it," added Mr. Aiken.
10109{_}2760{_}"You might be going to a party, so you might."
10109{_}2761{_}"I think," replied my father, "the evening will be more interesting than a purely social affair.
10109{_}2762{_}Keep the _Sea Tern_ well off, and we shall meet only too soon again.'
10109{_}2763{_}"Why don't I take the boy along," Mr. Aiken suggested, eyeing me a little furtively.
10109{_}2764{_}"He'd be right useful where we're going, and the sea would do him good, so it would."
10109{_}2765{_}"I fancy you'll have enough bother without him," replied my father.
10109{_}2766{_}"Personally I have found him quite distracting during my short visit."
10109{_}2767{_}"Hell," said Mr. Aiken, "he wouldn't be no trouble, but he looks fair ugly here, so he does, and he knows too much.
10109{_}2768{_}No offense, sir, but he's too up and coming to be left alone with an ignorant nigger."
10109{_}2769{_}My father shrugged his shoulders.
10109{_}2770{_}"Brutus is fond of the boy.
10109{_}2771{_}He will not hurt him."
10109{_}2772{_}"But the boy might hurt the nigger," said Mr. Aiken.
10109{_}2773{_}My father nodded blandly toward the hall.
10109{_}2774{_}"And you might be seasick," he said.
10109{_}2775{_}"Har," roared Mr. Aiken, seemingly struck by the subtle humor of the remark.
10109{_}2776{_}"Damned if you wouldn't joke if the deck was blowing off under you.
10109{_}2777{_}Damned if I ever seen the likes of you now, captain."
10109{_}2778{_}Still under the spell of mirth he left us.
10109{_}2779{_}The house door closed behind him, and Brutus glided into the room.
10109{_}2780{_}"Mademoiselle," said my father bowing, "I am sorry the cards have fallen so we must part.
10109{_}2781{_}If you had as few pleasant things as I to remember, you also might understand how poignantly I regret it, even though I know it is for the best.
10109{_}2782{_}It is time you were leaving such low company."
10109{_}2783{_}"I have found it pleasant sometimes," she replied a little wistfully.
10109{_}2784{_}"It takes very little to please me, captain."
10109{_}2785{_}"Sometimes," he replied, smiling, "anything is pleasant, but only sometimes.
10109{_}2786{_}Your brother has been notified, Mademoiselle.
10109{_}2787{_}You should hear from him in a little while now, when this hurry and bustle is over, and when you see him, give him my regards and my regrets.
10109{_}2788{_}And Mademoiselle" --he hesitated an instant--"would you think it insolent if I said I sometimes wished--Mon Dieu, Mademoiselle, do not take it so.
10109{_}2789{_}It was entirely unpardonable of me."
10109{_}2790{_}Mademoiselle had hidden her face in her hands.
10109{_}2791{_}My father, frowning slightly, rubbed his thumb along his sword blade.
10109{_}2792{_}"Forgive me, if you can," he said.
10109{_}2793{_}"I have often feared my manners would fail me sometime."
10109{_}2794{_}She looked up at him then, and her eyes were very bright.
10109{_}2795{_}"Suppose," she said softly, "I told you there was nothing to forgive.
10109{_}2796{_}Suppose I said--"  My father, bowing his lowest, politely and rather hastily interrupted.
10109{_}2797{_}"Mademoiselle would be too kind.
10109{_}2798{_}She would have forgotten that it is quite impossible."
10109{_}2799{_}"No," said Mademoiselle, shaking her head slowly, "it is not impossible.
10109{_}2800{_}You should have known better than to say that.
10109{_}2801{_}Suppose--" her voice choked a little, as though the words hurt her--"suppose I bade you recall, captain, what you said on the stairs at Blanzy, when they were at the door and you were going to meet them.
10109{_}2802{_}Do you remember?"
10109{_}2803{_}My father smiled, and made a polite little gesture of assumed despair.
10109{_}2804{_}Then his voice, very slow and cool, broke in on her speech and stilled it.
10109{_}2805{_}"Good God, Mademoiselle, one cannot remember everything."
10109{_}2806{_}Playing with the hilt of his sword, he stepped nearer, still smiling, still watching her with a polished curiosity.
10109{_}2807{_}"I have said so many little things to women in my time, so many little nothings.
10109{_}2808{_}It is hard to remember them all.
10109{_}2809{_}They have become confused now, and blended into an interesting background, whose elements I can no longer separate.
10109{_}2810{_}Your pardon, my lady, but I have forgotten, forgotten so completely that even the stairs seem merely a gentle blur."
10109{_}2811{_}And he pressed his hand over his brow and sighed, while he watched her face flush crimson.
10109{_}2812{_}"You lie!"
10109{_}2813{_}she cried.
10109{_}2814{_}"You have not forgotten!"
10109{_}2815{_}My father ceased to smile.
10109{_}2816{_}"And suppose I have not," he said.
10109{_}2817{_}"What is it to Mademoiselle?
10109{_}2818{_}What are the words of a ruined man, the idle speech of a fool who fancied he would sup that night in paradise, and what use is it to recall them now?
10109{_}2819{_}Is it possible you believe I am touched by such trivial matters?
10109{_}2820{_}Because everyone had done what you wish, do you think I shall also?
10109{_}2821{_}Do you think you can make me give up the paper, as though I were a simpering, romantic fool in Paris?
10109{_}2822{_}Do you think I have gone this far to turn back?
10109{_}2823{_}Mademoiselle seems to forget that I have the game in my own hands.
10109{_}2824{_}It would be a foolish thing to throw it all away, even--"  He paused, and bowed again.
10109{_}2825{_}"Even for you, Mademoiselle.
10109{_}2826{_}I have arrived where I am today only for one reason.
10109{_}2827{_}Can you not guess it?
10109{_}2828{_}It was a pleasure to take you from Blanzy.
10109{_}2829{_}It is business now, and they cannot be combined.
10109{_}2830{_}"Listen, Mademoiselle," he continued.
10109{_}2831{_}"Not three miles off the harbor mouth is a French ship tacking back and forth, and not entirely for pleasure.
10109{_}2832{_}Around this house at present are enough men to run your estates at Blanzy.
10109{_}2833{_}A sloop has come into the harbor this morning, and has landed its crew for my especial benefit.
10109{_}2834{_}A dozen of Napoleon's agents are waiting to spring at my throat.
10109{_}2835{_}I have succeeded so that there is not a man in town who would not be glad to see me on a yard arm.
10109{_}2836{_}And yet they are waiting, Mademoiselle.
10109{_}2837{_}Is it not amusing?
10109{_}2838{_}Can you guess why they are waiting?"
10109{_}2839{_}He took a pinch of snuff and dusted his fingers.
10109{_}2840{_}"Because they fear that I may burn the paper if they disturb me.
10109{_}2841{_}They believe if they keep hidden, if I do not suspect, that I may venture forth.
10109{_}2842{_}They hope to take me alive, or kill me, and still obtain the paper.
10109{_}2843{_}Indeed, it is their one hope.
10109{_}2844{_}It would be a pity to disappoint them."
10109{_}2845{_}His lips had parted, and his eyes were shining in the candle light.
10109{_}2846{_}"There are few things which move me now, my lady.
10109{_}2847{_}All that I really enjoy is an amusing situation, and this one is very amusing.
10109{_}2848{_}Do you think I have crossed the ocean to deliver this document, and then I shall stop?
10109{_}2849{_}No, Mademoiselle, you are mistaken."
10109{_}2850{_}He bowed again, and stepped backwards towards the door.
10109{_}2851{_}"Pray do likewise, Mademoiselle, and forget," he said.
10109{_}2852{_}"There is nothing in this little episode fit for you to remember.
10109{_}2853{_}It is not you they are after, and you will be quite safe here.
10109{_}2854{_}I have made sure of that.
10109{_}2855{_}My son will remain until your brother arrives, and will dispense what hospitality you require.
10109{_}2856{_}"I trust," he added, turning to me, "you still remember why you have been here?"
10109{_}2857{_}"Indeed, yes," I answered.
10109{_}2858{_}"Then it is good-bye, Henry.
10109{_}2859{_}I shall not bother to offer you my hand.
10109{_}2860{_}Brutus, you will remain with my son until a quarter to seven."
10109{_}2861{_}Even now I cannot tell what made a mist come over my eyes and a lump in my throat any more than I can explain my subsequent actions on that evening.
10109{_}2862{_}Was it possible I was sorry to see the last of him?
10109{_}2863{_}Or was it simply self pity that shortened my breath and made my voice seem broken and discordant?
10109{_}2864{_}"And after that?"
10109{_}2865{_}I asked.
10109{_}2866{_}He looked at me appraisingly, tapping his thin fingers on his sword hilt.
10109{_}2867{_}"After that--" He stared thoughtfully at the shadows of the darkened room.
10109{_}2868{_}Was he thinking as I was, of the wasted years and what the end would be?
10109{_}2869{_}"After that," he repeated, half to himself, "come, I will make an appointment with you after that--on the other side of the Styx, my son.
10109{_}2870{_}I shall be waiting there, I promise you, and we shall drink some corked ambrosia.
10109{_}2871{_}Surely the gods must give a little to the shades, or at any rate, Brutus shall steal some.
10109{_}2872{_}And then perhaps you shall tell me what happened after that.
10109{_}2873{_}I shall look forward--I shall hope, even, that it may be pleasant.
10109{_}2874{_}Good-bye, my son."
10109{_}2875{_}I think he had often planned that leave taking.
10109{_}2876{_}Surely it must have satisfied him.
10109{_}2877{_}XIII   He was gone, like the shades of which he had spoken, and Mademoiselle and I were left staring at the black rectangle of the broken door.
10109{_}2878{_}I drew a deep breath and looked about me quickly.
10109{_}2879{_}It seemed somehow as though a spell were broken, as though the curtain had lowered on some final act in the theatre.
10109{_}2880{_}Slowly my mind seemed to free itself from a hundred illusions, and to move along more logical paths.
10109{_}2881{_}Brutus went to the arms rack in the corner, and selected a rusted cutlass from the small arms that still rested there, thrust it at me playfully and grinned.
10109{_}2882{_}For a minute or even more, the single log that was still burning in the fireplace hissed drowsily, and I could hear the vines tapping gently on the windows.
10109{_}2883{_}Then I heard a pistol shot, followed by a hoarse cry.
10109{_}2884{_}Mademoiselle started to her feet, and then sank back in her chair again, and from where I was standing I could see that her face was white and her hands were trembling.
10109{_}2885{_}So she loved him.
10109{_}2886{_}My hand gripped hard against the back of a chair.
10109{_}2887{_}Why should I have hoped she did not?
10109{_}2888{_}"God!"
10109{_}2889{_}she gasped.
10109{_}2890{_}"I have killed him!"
10109{_}2891{_}"You?"
10109{_}2892{_}I cried, but she did not answer.
10109{_}2893{_}"Huh!"
10109{_}2894{_}said Brutus, and his grin grew broader.
10109{_}2895{_}"Monsieur's pistol.
10109{_}2896{_}He kill him."
10109{_}2897{_}"Indeed," I said, for the sense of unreality was still strong upon me.
10109{_}2898{_}"And whom did he kill, Brutus?"
10109{_}2899{_}Brutus cocked his head to one side, and listened.
10109{_}2900{_}Somewhere behind came a confusion of shouts and the thudding of horses' hoofs.
10109{_}2901{_}"He kill Mr. Jason Hill," said Brutus.
10109{_}2902{_}"Are you sure?"
10109{_}2903{_}Mademoiselle demanded sharply.
10109{_}2904{_}Brutus nodded, and the dull, fixed look went out of her eyes, and slowly a touch of color returned to her cheeks.
10109{_}2905{_}And then there was a clamor of voices and a tramp of feet and a crash on the door outside.
10109{_}2906{_}Brutus looked about him in wild indecision.
10109{_}2907{_}"We have callers," I observed, doing my best to keep my voice calm.
10109{_}2908{_}"Who are they, Brutus?"
10109{_}2909{_}Brutus, however, had forgotten me, and had sprung into the hall.
10109{_}2910{_}At almost the same instant, someone must have discovered that the door was unlocked, for a sudden draught eddied through the passage.
10109{_}2911{_}Then there was a confused babel of voices, to which I did not listen.
10109{_}2912{_}I was busy swinging up the sash of the nearest window.
10109{_}2913{_}"Quickly, Mademoiselle!"
10109{_}2914{_}I whispered.
10109{_}2915{_}"Damn it!"
10109{_}2916{_}someone shouted from the hall.
10109{_}2917{_}"There's another of 'em!"
10109{_}2918{_}And there came the crack of a pistol that echoed loudly in the passage.
10109{_}2919{_}"It is time we were going," I said.
10109{_}2920{_}"Out of the window, Mademoiselle!"
10109{_}2921{_}In my haste I almost pushed her from the sill to the lawn, and was leaning towards her.
10109{_}2922{_}"Mademoiselle, listen!
10109{_}2923{_}The stables are straight to the left.
10109{_}2924{_}Can you saddle a horse?"
10109{_}2925{_}She nodded.
10109{_}2926{_}"The first stall to the right.
10109{_}2927{_}I shall be there in an instant!"
10109{_}2928{_}For I remembered my sword, and sprang back into the room to get it.
10109{_}2929{_}"Get that man!"
10109{_}2930{_}someone was shouting.
10109{_}2931{_}"In after him, you fools!
10109{_}2932{_}Don't shoot in the dark!"
10109{_}2933{_}I had a glimpse of Brutus darting through the passage and making a leap for the stairs.
10109{_}2934{_}Then there was a crash of glass.
10109{_}2935{_}"Begad!"
10109{_}2936{_}came a hoarse voice.
10109{_}2937{_}"He's jumped clean through the window!"
10109{_}2938{_}And another pistol exploded from the landing above me.
10109{_}2939{_}"Five hundred dollars for the man who gets him."
10109{_}2940{_}I could swear I had heard the voice before.
10109{_}2941{_}"Damn it!
10109{_}2942{_}Don't let him go!
10109{_}2943{_}Out the door, all of you!
10109{_}2944{_}Out the door, men!
10109{_}2945{_}Out the door!"
10109{_}2946{_}There was a rush of feet through the passage.
10109{_}2947{_}I had a glimpse of men running past, and then I was half out the window.
10109{_}2948{_}"Stop!"
10109{_}2949{_}someone shouted.
10109{_}2950{_}I took a hasty glance behind me to find that my Uncle Jason had entered the morning room, his clothing torn and disarranged, the good nature erased from his face, and a gash on his left cheek that still was bleeding.
10109{_}2951{_}"Stop!"
10109{_}2952{_}he shouted again, "or I fire!"
10109{_}2953{_}Then I was out on the lawn with the cool air from the river on my face, and running for the stable.
10109{_}2954{_}I wonder what would have happened if the evening had been less far advanced, or the sky less overcast, or Mademoiselle less adroit than providence had made her.
10109{_}2955{_}She had bridled the horse and was swinging the saddle on him when I had reached the stable's shadow.
10109{_}2956{_}I could hear my uncle shouting for assistance as I tightened the girths, but Brutus must have led his men a pretty chase.
10109{_}2957{_}I mounted unmolested, as I somehow knew I should, and helped her up behind me.
10109{_}2958{_}Somehow with that first crash on our front door, I knew that the game had turned.
10109{_}2959{_}I knew that nothing would stop me.
10109{_}2960{_}An odd sense of exaltation came over me, and with it a strange desire to laugh.
10109{_}2961{_}It would be amusing enough when I met my father, but I wondered--I wondered as I clapped my heels into my horse's flanks.
10109{_}2962{_}What had my uncle to do in this affair?
10109{_}2963{_}XIV   It was just that time in an autumn day when the light is fading out of the sky.
10109{_}2964{_}The thick, heavy mists that the cold air encourages were rolling in chill and heavy from the river and leveling the hollow places in the land.
10109{_}2965{_}The clouds were still a claret colored purple in the west, but in another few minutes that color would be gone.
10109{_}2966{_}The shapes around us were fast losing their distinctiveness, and their outlines were becoming more and more a matter for the memory, and not the eye.
10109{_}2967{_}And it seems to me that I never knew the air to seem more fresh and sweet.
10109{_}2968{_}We had broken into a sharp gallop down the rutted lane.
10109{_}2969{_}The house, gaunt and spectral, and bleaker and more forbidding than the darkening sky, was behind us, and ahead were the broad level meadows, checkered with little clumps of willow and cedars, as meadows are that lie near the salt marshes.
10109{_}2970{_}I had feared we might be intercepted at our gate, but I was mistaken.
10109{_}2971{_}We had swerved to the left and were thudding down the level road, when an exclamation from Mademoiselle made me turn in my saddle.
10109{_}2972{_}My look must have been a somewhat blank interrogation, for Mademoiselle was laughing.
10109{_}2973{_}"To think," she cried, "I should have said you resembled your mother!
10109{_}2974{_}Where are we going, Monsieur?"
10109{_}2975{_}But I think she knew without my answering, for she laughed again, and I did not entirely blame her.
10109{_}2976{_}It was pleasant enough to leave our house behind.
10109{_}2977{_}It was pleasant to feel the bite of the salt wind, and to see the trees and the rocks by the roadside slip past us, gaunt and spectral in the evening.
10109{_}2978{_}I knew the road well enough, which was fortunate, even when we turned off the beaten track over a trail which was hardly as good as a foot path.
10109{_}2979{_}I was forced to reduce our pace to a walk, but I was confident that it did not make much difference.
10109{_}2980{_}Once on the path, the farm was not half a mile distant, just behind a ridge of rocks that was studded by a stunted undergrowth of wind beaten oak.
10109{_}2981{_}I knew the place.
10109{_}2982{_}I could already picture the gaping black windows, the broken, sagging ridge pole, and the crumbling chimney.
10109{_}2983{_}For years the wind had blown sighing through its deserted rooms, while the rain rotted the planking.
10109{_}2984{_}It was not strange that its owners had left it, for I can imagine no more mournful or desolate spot.
10109{_}2985{_}Our own house, three miles away, was its nearest neighbor, and scarcely a congenial one.
10109{_}2986{_}Around it was nothing but rain sogged meadows that scarcely rose above the salt marshes that ran to the dunes where the Atlantic was beating.
10109{_}2987{_}As I stared grimly ahead, I could picture her there behind me, the wind whipping the color to her cheeks and playing with her hair, her eyes bright and gay in the half-light.
10109{_}2988{_}Save for the steady plodding of the horse, it was very still.
10109{_}2989{_}I fancied that she had leaned nearer, that her shoulder was touching mine, that I could feel her breath on my cheek.
10109{_}2990{_}Then she spoke, and her voice was almost a whisper.
10109{_}2991{_}"It was good of you to take me with you," she said.
10109{_}2992{_}"Surely, Mademoiselle," I replied, "You did not think that I would leave you?"
10109{_}2993{_}"I should, if I had been you," she answered, "I was rude to you, Monsieur, and unjust to you this morning.
10109{_}2994{_}You see I did not know."
10109{_}2995{_}"You did not know?"
10109{_}2996{_}"That the son would be as brave and as resourceful as the father.
10109{_}2997{_}You are, Monsieur, and yet you are different."
10109{_}2998{_}"Yes," I said.
10109{_}2999{_}"And I am glad, glad," said Mademoiselle.
10109{_}3000{_}"And I am sorry you are glad," I said.
10109{_}3001{_}"You are sorry?"
10109{_}3002{_}"Perhaps, Mademoiselle," I replied with a tinge of bitterness I could not suppress, "if I had seen more of the world, if my clothes were in better taste, and my manners less abrupt--you would feel differently.

10109{_}4254{_}No, no," she added, as I started toward the door, "Stay here, Monsieur.
10109{_}4255{_}It is not your affair."
10109{_}4256{_}XVIII   She still stood looking at the pistols on the table.
10109{_}4257{_}Was she thinking, as I was, of the irony, and the comedy and the tragedy that had been so strangely blended in the last hour?
10109{_}4258{_}Slowly she turned and faced me, her slender fingers tugging aimlessly at her handkerchief.
10109{_}4259{_}For a moment her eyes met mine.
10109{_}4260{_}Then she looked away, and the color had deepened in her cheeks.
10109{_}4261{_}"So," said Mademoiselle, "It is almost over.
10109{_}4262{_}Are you not glad, Monsieur, that it is finished?"
10109{_}4263{_}The wick of a candle had dropped to the wax, and was spluttering fitfully.
10109{_}4264{_}Mechanically I moved to fix it.
10109{_}4265{_}"No," I said, "I am not glad."
10109{_}4266{_}"Not glad?
10109{_}4267{_}Surely you are glad it has ended so.
10109{_}4268{_}Surely you are glad your father--"  "No," I said, and my voice was so much louder than I had intended that the sound of it in the quiet room made me stop abruptly.
10109{_}4269{_}She looked up at me, a little startled.
10109{_}4270{_}"At least Monsieur is frank," she said.
10109{_}4271{_}"Do you know--have you thought that you are the only one of us who has been wholly so, who has not had something to conceal?
10109{_}4272{_}Pray go on, Monsieur.
10109{_}4273{_}It is pleasant to hear someone who is frank again.
10109{_}4274{_}Continue!
10109{_}4275{_}You must be glad for something.
10109{_}4276{_}Every cloud must have--do you not say--a silver lining?
10109{_}4277{_}If it is not your father--surely you are glad about me?"
10109{_}4278{_}She made a graceful little gesture of interrogation.
10109{_}4279{_}"Come, come," she went on, "You are not yourself tonight.
10109{_}4280{_}Never have I seen you look so black.
10109{_}4281{_}Think, Monsieur!
10109{_}4282{_}The men are on deck and the wind is fair.
10109{_}4283{_}Soon I shall be going.
10109{_}4284{_}Soon you will forget."
10109{_}4285{_}"No," I said, "Mademoiselle is mistaken.
10109{_}4286{_}I shall not forget."
10109{_}4287{_}"Nor I," she said gravely, "I wonder, Monsieur, if you understand--but you cannot understand what it has meant to me.
10109{_}4288{_}I have tried to tell you once before, but you are cold, like your father.
10109{_}4289{_}I have seen many men who have said gallant things, but only you two of all I know have done them."
10109{_}4290{_}"I have done nothing," I said.
10109{_}4291{_}"You know I have done nothing."
10109{_}4292{_}"But it has not been your fault," she answered.
10109{_}4293{_}"And was it nothing to protect a stranger from a strange land, when you had nothing to gain from it and everything to lose?"
10109{_}4294{_}"Mademoiselle forgets," I said, "that I had nothing to lose.
10109{_}4295{_}It was lost already."
10109{_}4296{_}"Then surely," she replied lightly, "surely you must be glad I am going?"
10109{_}4297{_}"You know better than that," I answered.
10109{_}4298{_}"Ah, Mademoiselle, do you not see?
10109{_}4299{_}I hoped I might show you that I did not always blunder.
10109{_}4300{_}I hoped I might show you--"  The words seemed to choke me.
10109{_}4301{_}"Ah, Mademoiselle," I cried, "if I had only been on the stairs at Blanzy!"
10109{_}4302{_}"Blanzy!"
10109{_}4303{_}she echoed, "Pray what has Blanzy to do with you and me?"
10109{_}4304{_}Even now I do not know what made me speak, save that she was going.
10109{_}4305{_}The very ticking of the clock was bringing the moment nearer, and there she was, staring at me, wide-eyed, half puzzled and half frightened.
10109{_}4306{_}It seemed already as though she were further away.
10109{_}4307{_}"Do you not see?"
10109{_}4308{_}I said.
10109{_}4309{_}"It is not like you not to understand.
10109{_}4310{_}Nor is it very kind.
10109{_}4311{_}How can I see you go and be glad?
10109{_}4312{_}How can I be glad you love my father?"
10109{_}4313{_}"Mon Dieu!"
10109{_}4314{_}she exclaimed suddenly startled, "Your father!
10109{_}4315{_}I care for your father!"
10109{_}4316{_}I bowed in quick contrition.
10109{_}4317{_}"Mademoiselle," I said, "I fear I have been very rude, and, as usual, very gauche.
10109{_}4318{_}I beg you to forgive me."
10109{_}4319{_}"But I tell you," she cried, "I do not love him!"
10109{_}4320{_}I bowed again in silence.
10109{_}4321{_}"You do not believe me?"
10109{_}4322{_}"Mademoiselle may rest assured," I replied gently, "that I understand--perfectly."
10109{_}4323{_}"You!"
10109{_}4324{_}I started at her sudden vexation, started to find that her eyes were filled with tears.
10109{_}4325{_}"You understand quite nothing!
10109{_}4326{_}Never have I seen anyone so cruel, so stupid!"
10109{_}4327{_}"Mademoiselle," I said, "I have been awkward, but forgive me--the cabin of the _Sea Tern_, where you asked him to sail on, and when you bade him recall what he said on the stairs at Blanzy....
10109{_}4328{_}Your pardon!
10109{_}4329{_}I have been very blunt."
10109{_}4330{_}And now she was regarding me with blank astonishment.
10109{_}4331{_}"Surely he told you," she murmured, "Surely he told you what the Marquis had intended."
10109{_}4332{_}Then she stopped, confused and silent.
10109{_}4333{_}"Mon Dieu!"
10109{_}4334{_}she exclaimed suddenly, "But he has told you nothing!"
10109{_}4335{_}"No," I said dully, "He has been most discreet.
10109{_}4336{_}But does it make any real difference, Mademoiselle, except that I know now that the Marquis was a man of very keen discrimination?"
10109{_}4337{_}"Are you mad?"
10109{_}4338{_}cried Mademoiselle, "I tell you it is not your father.
10109{_}4339{_}I tell you I--"  Her face had grown scarlet.
10109{_}4340{_}She bowed her head, and tugged more violently than ever at the corner of her handkerchief.
10109{_}4341{_}"Mademoiselle," I said unsteadily, "Mademoiselle, what was it he told you at Blanzy?"
10109{_}4342{_}"I cannot tell you if you do not know," she answered, "Indeed I cannot."
10109{_}4343{_}"But you will!"
10109{_}4344{_}I cried.
10109{_}4345{_}"You will, Mademoiselle!
10109{_}4346{_}You must!
10109{_}4347{_}Mademoiselle--"  Her eyes had met mine again.
10109{_}4348{_}"They were breaking in the door," she began, "and he was going down to meet them.
10109{_}4349{_}I told him--I told him to go, to leave me, and take the paper.
10109{_}4350{_}He said--"  She paused again, watching me in vague embarrassment.
10109{_}4351{_}"He said he'd be damned if he would, Monsieur.
10109{_}4352{_}He said he would do what the Marquis had directed, if he had to swing for it.
10109{_}4353{_}That he would take the paper and me to America--that I ... Mon Dieu!
10109{_}4354{_}Do you not know what he said!
10109{_}4355{_}Can you not guess?...
10109{_}4356{_}He said that I was to marry his son."
10109{_}4357{_}A smile suddenly played about her lips.
10109{_}4358{_}"And I told him," she continued breathlessly, "I told him I'd be damned if I would, Monsieur.
10109{_}4359{_}That neither he nor the Marquis would make me marry a man I did not know, much less a son of his!"
10109{_}4360{_}"And when you asked him to recall it--Mademoiselle, when you asked him to recall it, did you mean--tell me, Mademoiselle!"
10109{_}4361{_}"Ah," she whispered, "but it is too soon, and you are too rough, Monsieur!
10109{_}4362{_}I beg of you--be careful!
10109{_}4363{_}Besides--someone is coming."
10109{_}4364{_}And then I heard a soft footstep behind me.
10109{_}4365{_}"Huh!"
10109{_}4366{_}said Brutus, "I go tell the captain.
10109{_}4367{_}No.
10109{_}4368{_}It is all right.
10109{_}4369{_}I tell the captain.
10109{_}4370{_}He is happy.
10109{_}4371{_}It will please him.
10109{_}4372{_}Huh!"
10109{_}4373{_}His long speech seemed to have taken his breath, for he paused, grinning broadly.
10109{_}4374{_}"Huh!"
10109{_}4375{_}he said finally.
10109{_}4376{_}"Mr. Lawton shoot Mr. Jason.
10109{_}4377{_}Shoot him with pistol off the table.
10109{_}4378{_}The captain is happy."
10109{_}4379{_}But before Brutus could turn to go, my father was in the doorway, smoothing the bandage on his arm.
10109{_}4380{_}"Let us say relieved, Brutus," he answered smoothly.
10109{_}4381{_}"It is dangerous ever to use superlatives."
10109{_}4382{_}Then he glanced from Mademoiselle to me, and his smile broadened.
10109{_}4383{_}"Very much relieved," he said, "and yet--and yet I still feel thirsty.
10109{_}4384{_}The rum decanter, Brutus."
